                                  function simpleMask(str, key) {
                                      var result = ''; 
                                      for (var i = 0; i < str.length; ++i)
                                          result += String.fromCharCode(key ^ str.charCodeAt(i));
                                      return result;
                                  }

               <div class="msg-210x60" data-format="210x60" data-type="ad" data-publisher="lqm.codeproject.site" data-zone="General-Programming/String-handling/Strings" data-tags="VS.NET2003, C#, Windows, .NET, Visual-Studio, HTML, Dev, Intermediate, VS2010,rating4.5">

                 <a href="https://pubads.g.doubleclick.net/gampad/jump?iu=/6839/lqm.codeproject.site/General-Programming/String-handling/Strings&amp;sz=210x60&amp;c=624125"><img src="https://pubads.g.doubleclick.net/gampad/jump?iu=/6839/lqm.codeproject.site/General-Programming/String-handling/Strings&amp;sz=210x60&amp;c=624125" width="210px" height="60px" target="_blank"></a>

             <div id="ctl00_description" class="summary">
              Parsing PDF files in .NET using PDFBox and IKVM.NET (managed code).
             </div>
             <span id="ctl00_thumbnailUrl" class="date" content="https://www.codeproject.com/script/Articles/Images/article100x80.png"></span> 
            </div> 
            <div id="contentdiv" class="text"> 
             <ul class="download"> 
              <li><a href="/KB/string/pdf2text/Pdf2Text.Small.20150420.zip">Download source files - 82 kB</a> [codeproject.com]</li> 
              <li><a href="http://www.squarepdf.net/how-to-convert-pdf-to-text-in-net">Download full project including all dependencies</a> [squarepdf.net]</li> 
             </ul> 
             <h2>Update</h2> 
             <p><em>April 20, 2015:</em>&nbsp;The article and the Visual Studio project are updated and work with the latest PDFBox version (1.8.9). It's also possible to download the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.squarepdf.net/how-to-convert-pdf-to-text-in-net-sample-project">project with all dependencies</a>&nbsp;(resolving the dependencies proved to be a bit tricky).</p> 
             <p><em>February 27, 2014:</em> This article originally described parsing PDF files using PDFBox. It has been extended to include samples for IFilter and iTextSharp.</p> 
             <p><span style="color: rgb(255, 153, 0); font-size: 30px">How to Parse PDF Files</span></p> 
             <p>There are several main methods for extracting text from PDF files in .NET:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Microsoft IFilter interface and Adobe IFilter implementation.</li> 
              <li>iTextSharp</li> 
              <li>PDFBox</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>None of these PDF parsing solutions is perfect. We will discuss all these methods below.</p> 
             <h2>1. Parsing PDF using Adobe PDF IFilter</h2> 
             <p>In order to parse PDF files using IFilter interface you need the following:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Windows 2000 or later</li> 
              <li>Adobe Acrobat or Reader 7.0.5+ (or the standalone <a href="http://www.adobe.com/support/downloads/detail.jsp?ftpID=2611" target="_blank">Adobe PDF IFilter</a> [adobe.com])</li> 
              <li><a href="http://www.dotlucene.net/78726/how-to-extract-text-from-microsoft-office-documents-doc-xls">IFilter COM wrapper class</a> [dotlucene.net]</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>Sample code:</p> 
             <pre><span class="code-keyword">using</span> IFilter;

<span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> ...</span>

<span class="code-keyword">public</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">string</span> ExtractTextFromPdf(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> path) {
  <span class="code-keyword">return</span> DefaultParser.Extract(path); 
} </pre> 
             <p>Download a sample project:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><a href="http://www.squarepdf.net/parsing-pdf-files-using-ifilter-c-net">Parsing PDF Files using IFilter</a> [squarepdf.net]</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>If you are using the PDF IFilter that comes with Adobe Acrobat Reader you will need to rename the process to "<span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0); font-family: &quot;Open Sans&quot;, Tahoma, Geneva, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 13px">filtdump.exe" otherwise the IFilter interface will return </span>E_NOTIMPL error code. See more at <a href="http://www.squarepdf.net/parsing-pdf-files-using-ifilter-c-net">Parsing PDF Files using IFilter</a> [squarepdf.net].</p> 
             <p>Disadvantages:</p> 
             <ol> 
              <li>Using unreliable COM interop that handles IFilter interface (and the combination of IFilter COM and Adobe PDF IFilter is especially troublesome).</li> 
              <li>A separate installation of Adobe IFilter on the target system. This can be painful if you need to distribute your indexing solution to someone else.</li> 
              <li>You have to use "filtdump.exe" file name for your application with the latest PDF IFilter implementation that comes with Acrobat Reader.</li> 
             </ol> 
             <h2>2. Parsing PDF using iTextSharp</h2> 
             <p><a href="http://sourceforge.net/projects/itextsharp/" target="_blank">iTextSharp</a> is a .NET port of <a href="http://itextpdf.com/" target="_blank">iText</a>, a PDF manipulation library for Java. It is primarily focused on creating and not reading PDFs but it supports extracting text from PDF as well.</p> 
             <p>Sample code:</p> 
             <pre><span class="code-keyword">using</span> iTextSharp.text.pdf;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> iTextSharp.text.pdf.parser;

<span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> ...</span>
 
<span class="code-keyword">public</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">string</span> ExtractTextFromPdf(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> path)
{
  <span class="code-keyword">using</span> (PdfReader reader = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PdfReader(path))
  {
    StringBuilder text = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> StringBuilder();

    <span class="code-keyword">for</span> (<span class="code-keyword">int</span> i = <span class="code-digit">1</span>; i <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= reader.NumberOfPages; i++)
    {
        text.Append(PdfTextExtractor.GetTextFromPage(reader, i));
    }

    <span class="code-keyword">return</span> text.ToString();
  }
} </pre> 
             <p>Credit: <a href="http://www.codeproject.com/Messages/4767278/iTextSharp.aspx">Member 10364982</a></p> 
             <p>Download a sample project:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><a href="http://www.squarepdf.net/parsing-pdf-files-using-itextsharp">Parsing PDF Files using iTextSharp</a> [squarepdf.net]</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>You may consider using <strong>LocationTextExtractionStrategy</strong> to get better precision.</p> 
             <pre><span class="code-keyword">public</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">string</span> ExtractTextFromPdf(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> path)
{
  ITextExtractionStrategy its = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> iTextSharp.text.pdf.parser.LocationTextExtractionStrategy();
  
  <span class="code-keyword">using</span> (PdfReader reader = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PdfReader(path))
  {
      StringBuilder text = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> StringBuilder();

      <span class="code-keyword">for</span> (<span class="code-keyword">int</span> i = <span class="code-digit">1</span>; i <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= reader.NumberOfPages; i++)
      {
          <span class="code-keyword">string</span> thePage = PdfTextExtractor.GetTextFromPage(reader, i, its);
          string[] theLines = thePage.Split(<span class="code-string">'</span><span class="code-string">\n'</span>);
          <span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (<span class="code-keyword">var</span> theLine <span class="code-keyword">in</span> theLines)
          {
              text.AppendLine(theLine);
          }
      }
      <span class="code-keyword">return</span> text.ToString();
  }
}  </pre> 
             <p>&nbsp;</p> 
             <p>Credit: <a href="http://www.codeproject.com/Messages/4772133/Re-iTextSharp-suggestion-and-problem.aspx">Member 10140900</a></p> 
             <p>Disadvantages of iTextSharp:</p> 
             <ol> 
              <li>Licensing if you are not happy with <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affero_General_Public_License">AGPL license</a></li> 
             </ol> 
             <h2>3. Parsing PDF using PDFBox</h2> 
             <p><a href="http://pdfbox.apache.org/" target="_blank">PDFBox</a> is another Java PDF library. It is also ready to be used with the original Java Lucene (see <a href="http://pdfbox.apache.org/apidocs/org/apache/pdfbox/searchengine/lucene/LucenePDFDocument.html" target="_blank">LucenePDFDocument</a>).</p> 
             <p>Fortunately, there is a .NET version of PDFBox that is created using <a href="http://www.ikvm.net/" target="_blank">IKVM.NET</a> (just <a href="http://www.squarepdf.net/pdfbox-in-net/" target="_blank">download the PDFBox package</a>).</p> 
             <p>Using PDFBox in .NET requires adding references to:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>IKVM.OpenJDK.Core.dll</li> 
              <li>IKVM.OpenJDK.SwingAWT.dll</li> 
              <li>pdfbox-1.8.9.dll</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>and copying the following files the <em>bin</em> directory:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>commons-logging.dll</li> 
              <li>fontbox-1.8.9.dll</li> 
              <li>IKVM.OpenJDK.Text.dll</li> 
              <li>IKVM.OpenJDK.Util.dll</li> 
              <li>IKVM.Runtime.dll</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>Using the PDFBox to parse PDFs is fairly easy:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">using</span> org.apache.pdfbox.pdmodel;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> org.apache.pdfbox.util;

<span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> ...</span>

<span class="code-keyword">private</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">string</span> ExtractTextFromPdf(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> path)
{
  PDDocument doc = <span class="code-keyword">null</span>;
  <span class="code-keyword">try</span> {
    doc = PDDocument.load(path)
    PDFTextStripper stripper = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PDFTextStripper();
    <span class="code-keyword">return</span> stripper.getText(doc);
  }
  <span class="code-keyword">finally</span> {
    <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (doc != <span class="code-keyword">null</span>) {
      doc.close();
    }
  }
}  </pre> 
             <p>Download a sample project:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><a href="http://www.squarepdf.net/how-to-convert-pdf-to-text-in-net">How to convert PDF files to text in C# (.NET)</a> [squarepdf.net]</li> 
              <li><a href="http://www.squarepdf.net/how-to-convert-pdf-to-text-in-net-vb">How to convert PDF file to text in VB (.NET)</a> [squarepdf.net]</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>The size of the required assemblies adds up to almost 18 MB:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>IKVM.OpenJDK.Core.dll (4 MB)</li> 
              <li>IKVM.OpenJDK.SwingAWT.dll (6 MB)</li> 
              <li>pdfbox-1.8.9.dll (4 MB)</li> 
              <li>commons-logging.dll (82 kB)</li> 
              <li>fontbox-1.8.9.dll (180 kB)</li> 
              <li>IKVM.OpenJDK.Text.dll (800 kB)</li> 
              <li>IKVM.OpenJDK.Util.dll (2 MB)</li> 
              <li>IKVM.Runtime.dll (1 MB)</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>The speed is not so bad: Parsing the <a href="http://www.copyright.gov/title17/circ92.pdf" target="_blank">U.S. Copyright Act PDF</a> (5.1 MB) took about 13 seconds.</p> 
             <p>Thanks to <a href="http://www.codeproject.com/Messages/4767914/The-sample-code.aspx">bobrien100</a> for improvements suggestions.</p> 
             <p>Disadvantages:</p> 
             <ol> 
              <li>IKVM.NET Dependencies (18 MB)</li> 
              <li>Speed (especially the IKVM.NET warm-up time)</li> 
             </ol>

                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl30269551.SwitchMessage(null,5301519);" href="/Messages/5301519/How-I-retrieve-the-text-was-extracted-from-the-pdf.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>if you used this example <br> &nbsp; <pre lang="C#"><span class="code-keyword">using</span> System;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> System.IO;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> org.apache.pdfbox.pdmodel;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> org.apache.pdfbox.util;
&nbsp;
<span class="code-keyword">namespace</span> Pdf2Text
{
    <span class="code-keyword">class</span> Program
    {
        <span class="code-summarycomment">///</span><span class="code-comment"> <span class="code-summarycomment">&lt;</span><span class="code-summarycomment">summary</span><span class="code-summarycomment">&gt;</span>
</span>        <span class="code-summarycomment">///</span><span class="code-comment"> The main entry point for the application.
</span>        <span class="code-summarycomment">///</span><span class="code-comment"> <span class="code-summarycomment">&lt;</span><span class="code-summarycomment">/summary</span><span class="code-summarycomment">&gt;</span>
</span>        [STAThread]
        <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> Main(string[] args)
        {
            DateTime start = DateTime.Now;
            <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (args.Length <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span> <span class="code-digit">2</span>)
            {
                Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">Usage: PDF2TEXT &lt;input filename (PDF)&gt; &lt;output filename (text)&gt;"</span>);
                <span class="code-keyword">return</span>;
            }
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-keyword">using</span> (StreamWriter sw = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> StreamWriter(args[1]))
            {
                sw.WriteLine(parseUsingPDFBox(args[0]));
            }
&nbsp;
            Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">Done. Took "</span> + (DateTime.Now - start));
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment">          Console.ReadLine();</span>
&nbsp;
        }
&nbsp;
        <span class="code-keyword">private</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">string</span> parseUsingPDFBox(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> input)
        {
            PDDocument doc = <span class="code-keyword">null</span>;
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-keyword">try</span>
            {
                doc = PDDocument.load(input);
                PDFTextStripper stripper = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PDFTextStripper();
                <span class="code-keyword">return</span> stripper.getText(doc);
            }
            <span class="code-keyword">finally</span>
            {
                <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (doc != <span class="code-keyword">null</span>)
                {
                    doc.close();
                }
            }
        }
    }
}</pre> <br> then you need to supply 2 arguments, the pdf file and a file to receive the text - you can also change the output to not use the streamwriter but to do something like <br> &nbsp; <pre lang="C#">Console.WriteLine(parseUsingPDFBox(args[0]));</pre> <br> or if you want to debug<br> &nbsp; <pre lang="C#"><span class="code-sdkkeyword">String</span> pdfIntoString = parseUsingPDFBox(args[0]);</pre> <br> and step through the program in debug mode/use a breakpoint on that line and check wether pdfIntoString ends up with any content<br></td> 
                             </tr>

                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:38px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="468369" msgid="5047545" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="38px" alt=""></td>
                      <td class="text">
                       <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="5px" width="100%">

                         <tr> 
                          <td>
                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                            <tbody>
                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl30269551.SwitchMessage(null,5045057);" href="/Messages/5045057/Non-Unicode-Characters.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>Unfortunately I'm not able to help much here. Extracting non-ASCII text from PDF files is a pain.<br> <br> As far as I know, earlier versions of the PDF format (such as 1.4) which are still in wide use didn't support Unicode and you needed to use specific pre-unicode encoding (like Windows-1253). Which makes it difficult during text extraction because it has to be mapped properly. If the library of your choice doesn't do that you can hardly improve it yourself.<br> &nbsp; 
                               <div class="signature">
                                --
                                <br> My open-source AJAX controls:
                                <br> 
                                <a href="http://javascript.daypilot.org/">DayPilot for JavaScript/HTML5/jQuery</a> - Calendar/Scheduling Control for JavaScript
                                <br> 
                                <a href="http://www.daypilot.org/">DayPilot for ASP.NET</a> - Calendar/Scheduling Control for ASP.NET WebForms
                                <br> 
                                <a href="http://mvc.daypilot.org/">DayPilot for MVC</a> - Calendar/Scheduling Control for ASP.NET MVC
                                <br> 
                                <a href="http://java.daypilot.org/">DayPilot for Java</a> - Calendar/Scheduling Control for Java
                                <br> 
                               </div><br></td>

                      <td class="subject hover-container"><a class="message-link" name="4776795" parent="0" thread="4776795" href="/Messages/4776795/Free-GNU-xpdf-library-to-extract-text.aspx">Free (GNU) xpdf library to extract text</a> <a onclick="return forumControl30269551.Pin(this);" rel="nofollow" href="#" title="Click to pin message"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/pin.png" border="0" align="top" alt="Pin" width="13px" height="13px"></a>

                 <tr id="F4776795_h1" class="content root selected" style="display:none;"> 
                  <td class="normal" width="100%">
                   <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%">

                     <tr valign="top"> 
                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:20px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="581802" msgid="4776795" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="20px" alt=""></td>
                      <td class="text">
                       <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="5px" width="100%"> 
                        <tbody>
                         <tr> 
                          <td>
                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                            <tbody>
                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">There is also the xpdf library which contains a small exe named pdftotext.exe, this program will output all the text to a text file. It will try to rebuild the original pdf layout.<br> You can download it from <a href="http://www.foolabs.com/xpdf/download.html">Xpdf: Download</a>.<br> I used it in a solution as it was much simpler than the options mentioned here which are too heavy to handle.<br> A usage example is: pdftotext.exe -layout -eol dos -end UTF-8 File.pdf File.txt<br> then you can read the text file or better capture it directly.<br> <br> If you are using C++ you can have a look at mupdf or podofo but for this last one be ready to spend sometimes to get it working.<br></td> 
                             </tr>

                               </div>i tried PdfLib from <a href="http://www.pdflib.com/download/tet/">http://www.pdflib.com/download/tet/</a>[<a href="http://www.pdflib.com/download/tet/" target="_blank" title="New Window">^</a>]<br> <br> and it outputs the right text file for me(unicode of the special characters is there)<br> <br> the description of tet says:<br> 
                               <blockquote class="FQ">
                                <div class="FQA">
                                 Quote:
                                </div>Since text in PDF is usually not encoded in Unicode, PDFlib TET normalizes the text in a PDF document to Unicode:
                                <br> 
                                <br> TET converts all text contents to Unicode. In C and other non-Unicode aware languages the text is returned in the UTF-8 or UTF-16 formats, and as native strings in Unicode-capable programming languages.
                                <br> 
                                <br> Ligatures and other multi-character glyphs are decomposed into a sequence of the corresponding Unicode characters.
                                <br> 
                                <br> 
                                <b>Glyphs without appropriate Unicode mappings are identified as such, and are mapped to a configurable replacement character in order to avoid misinterpretation.</b>
                                <br> 
                                <br> TET implements various workarounds for problems with specific document creation packages, such as InDesign and TeX documents or PDFs generated on mainframe systems.

                      <td class="subject hover-container"><a class="message-link" name="4771038" parent="4771029" thread="4771029" href="/Messages/4771038/Re-iTextSharp-suggestion-and-problem.aspx">Re: iTextSharp suggestion and problem</a> <a onclick="return forumControl30269551.Pin(this);" rel="nofollow" href="#" title="Click to pin message"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/pin.png" border="0" align="top" alt="Pin" width="13px" height="13px"></a>

                     <tr valign="top"> 
                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:38px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="468369" msgid="4771038" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="38px" alt=""></td>
                      <td class="text">
                       <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="5px" width="100%"> 
                        <tbody>
                         <tr> 
                          <td>
                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                            <tbody>
                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl30269551.SwitchMessage(null,4771029);" href="/Messages/4771029/iTextSharp-suggestion-and-problem.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>Please see the updated code:<br> <br> <pre><span class="code-keyword">using</span> iTextSharp.text.pdf;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> iTextSharp.text.pdf.parser;
&nbsp;
<span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> ...</span>
 
<span class="code-keyword">public</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">string</span> ExtractTextFromPdf(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> path)
{
  <span class="code-keyword">using</span> (PdfReader reader = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PdfReader(path))
  {
    StringBuilder text = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> StringBuilder();
&nbsp;
    <span class="code-keyword">for</span> (<span class="code-keyword">int</span> i = <span class="code-digit">1</span>; i <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= reader.NumberOfPages; i++)
    {
        text.Append(PdfTextExtractor.GetTextFromPage(reader, i));
    }
&nbsp;
    <span class="code-keyword">return</span> text.ToString();
  }
} </pre><br> <br> The <b>PdfReader class</b> can be found in iTextSharp.text.pdf namespace.<br>

                               </div>Thanks; czech it out, I get it working with your help with this code:<br> <br> private void button1_Click(object sender, EventArgs e)<br> {<br> string s = ExtractTextFromPdf(@"C:\MiscInWindows7\Tom Sawyer 1.pdf");<br> MessageBox.Show(s);<br> }<br> <br> public static String ExtractTextFromPdf(string path)<br> {<br> using (PdfReader reader = new PdfReader(path))<br> {<br> StringBuilder text = new StringBuilder();<br> <br> for (int i = 1; i &lt;= reader.NumberOfPages; i++)<br> {<br> text.Append(PdfTextExtractor.GetTextFromPage(reader, i));<br> }<br> <br> return text.ToString();<br> }<br> } <br> <br> But unfortunately, the lines returned from PDF files are often just one word, instead of an entire sentence.                       <td class="subject hover-container"><a class="message-link" name="4771062" parent="4771044" thread="4771029" href="/Messages/4771062/Re-iTextSharp-suggestion-and-problem.aspx">Re: iTextSharp suggestion and problem</a> <a onclick="return forumControl30269551.Pin(this);" rel="nofollow" href="#" title="Click to pin message"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/pin.png" border="0" align="top" alt="Pin" width="13px" height="13px"></a>

                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:74px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="468369" msgid="4771062" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="74px" alt=""></td>
                      <td class="text">

                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl30269551.SwitchMessage(null,4771044);" href="/Messages/4771044/Re-iTextSharp-suggestion-and-problem.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>Well, PDF is not a format that supports a good text flow. Its structure is more similar to object graphics format like SVG rather than text format like HTML.<br> <br> The text output quality depends a lot on the quality of the input PDF file. It's not unusual to see paragraphs stored as individual lines of text. Sometimes the full page is stored as image which makes it unreadable for text-based extractors like this example (you would have to use OCR).<br> <br> The output of the extracting methods is suitable as input for indexing engines - it outputs words, usually as fragments of a paragraph. You only get paragraphs if you are lucky.<br> <br> You can try the PDFBox library (the third option in this article). People report better results in terms of text consistency. It's slower that iTextSharp but that usually doesn't matter much.<br>

                       <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="5px" width="100%">

                         <tr>

                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%">

                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl30269551.SwitchMessage(null,4771062);" href="/Messages/4771062/Re-iTextSharp-suggestion-and-problem.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>You can use the LocationTextExecutionStrategy class as recommended here:<br> <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/8442327/reading-pdf-file-using-itextsharp#">http://stackoverflow.com/questions/8442327/reading-pdf-file-using-itextsharp#</a><br> <br> to get a more exact parsing of the pdf with carriage returns.<br> Here is some code which seems to work ok:<br> <br> <pre lang="c#">        <span class="code-keyword">public</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">string</span> ExtractTextFromPdf(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> path)
        {
            ITextExtractionStrategy its = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> iTextSharp.text.pdf.parser.LocationTextExtractionStrategy();
            
            <span class="code-keyword">using</span> (PdfReader reader = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PdfReader(path))
            {
                StringBuilder text = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> StringBuilder();
&nbsp;
                <span class="code-keyword">for</span> (<span class="code-keyword">int</span> i = <span class="code-digit">1</span>; i <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= reader.NumberOfPages; i++)
                {
                    <span class="code-keyword">string</span> thePage = PdfTextExtractor.GetTextFromPage(reader, i, its);
                    string[] theLines = thePage.Split(<span class="code-string">'</span><span class="code-string">\n'</span>);
                    <span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (<span class="code-keyword">var</span> theLine <span class="code-keyword">in</span> theLines)
                    {
                        text.AppendLine(theLine);
                    }
                }
                <span class="code-keyword">return</span> text.ToString();
            }
        } </pre><br> <br> I suppose you could replace the \n with \r\n in the page and that might work too.<br></td>

                              <td colspan="2">The code example is good however it is not intuitively obvious where the PDDocument class and PDFTextStripper come from. The following namespaces should be included in your code...<br> <br> <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">using</span> org.apache.pdfbox.pdmodel;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> org.apache.pdfbox.util;</pre><br> <br> Putting the "doc.close();" statement in a finally block is probably a good idea, too. <br> <br> Other than that, this article is useful and informative. Thank you!<br></td>

                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:20px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="10364982" msgid="4767278" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="20px" alt=""></td>
                      <td class="text">
                       <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="5px" width="100%"> 
                        <tbody>
                         <tr> 
                          <td>
                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                            <tbody>
                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">Getting text from PDF using iTextSharp is simple as it has a PdfTextExtractor class with the GetTextFromPage method. A simple for loop over the pages gets all the text as you would expect it. We use if for exactly this same job.<br> <br> <pre lang="c#"><span class="code-keyword">using</span> iTextSharp.text.pdf.parser;
&nbsp;
        <span class="code-keyword">public</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-sdkkeyword">String</span> ExtractText( PdfReader reader )
        {
            StringBuilder text = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> StringBuilder();
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-sdkkeyword">Int32</span> pages = reader.NumberOfPages;
            <span class="code-keyword">for</span> ( <span class="code-keyword">int</span> i = <span class="code-digit">1</span>; i <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= pages; i++ )
            {
                text.Append( PdfTextExtractor.GetTextFromPage( reader, i ) );
            }
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-keyword">return</span> text.ToString();
        }</pre><br></td> 
                             </tr>

So you just can copy this example method into any class of your making.                         function getVotesHistogram(objectId, objectTypeId, containerId, loadingId) {
                            if (!$('#' + containerId).attr('alreadyRequested')){
                                $.ajax({
                                    url: '/script/Ratings/Ajax/Histogram.aspx?obid=' + objectId + '&obtid='+objectTypeId,
                                    success: function (data) {
                                        $('#' + containerId).html(data);
                                        $('#' + loadingId).hide();
                                    }
                                });
                                $('#' + containerId).attr('alreadyRequested', 'true');
                            }
                        }
